Ibn Hajar al-Haytami: A Shafi'i Reference in Fatwa Practice
Biography of the Shafi'i jurist known for his Fatawa Kubra

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key biographical facts of Ibn Hajar al-Haytami and explain why his fatwa collection is consulted in Hanafi fatwa practice.

Core Idea
A Shafi'i scholar whose fatwa collection is a cross-madhhab reference for fatwa practitioners.

This lesson introduces a scholar whose name is often encountered in fatwa literature. Although he belonged to the Shafi'i school, his Fatawa Kubra is consulted by scholars of all schools for its thorough analysis. Knowing his biography helps you place his fatwas in context and avoid confusion with the earlier hadith scholar Ibn Hajar al-Asqalani.

Guided Path
1
Identify full name and titles
Start by noting the full name: Shaykh al-Islam Shihab al-Din Ahmad bin Muhammad bin 'Ali, 'Allamah Ibn Hajar al-Haytami. Each title indicates his scholarly rank.
The title 'Shaykh al-Islam' reflects his high status.
2
Note birthplace and death place
He was born in Abu al-Haytam, Egypt, hence 'al-Haytami'. He died in Mecca, hence 'al-Makki'. These nisbas distinguish him from other scholars.
His death in Mecca is why he is also called al-Makki.
3
Distinguish from Ibn Hajar al-Asqalani
He lived roughly half a century after the famous hadith commentator Ibn Hajar al-Asqalani (d. 852 AH). They are different individuals with different specializations.
This is a common source of confusion.
4
Recognize his major fatwa work
His primary work is Fatawa Kubra (also called Fatawa Haytamiyah), a four-volume collection. It is widely used across madhhabs.
Despite being Shafi'i, it is a valuable comparative resource.
5
Understand his relevance across madhhabs
Hanafi muftis often consult his Fatawa Kubra for fatwa formulation, especially when addressing issues not explicitly covered in Hanafi primary sources or for comparative insight.
This enriches the fatwa and demonstrates inter-madhhab benefit.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
شیخ الاسلام شہاب الدین احمد بن محمد بن علی علامہ ابن حجر هیتمی اور پیشی کمکی رحمہ اللہ ( ۹ ۹ فر ۹۷۳ھ ) جلیل القدر شافعی فقیہ ہیں ۔ ولادت مصر میں ابوا ہیتم نامی محلہ میں ہوئی تھی اس لیے بیتمی سے مشہور ہوئے وفات مکہ مکرمہ میں ہوئی ہے اس لیے مکی بھی کہلاتے ہیں۔ حافظ ابن حجر عسقلانی رحمہ اللہ (۷۷۳ ف ۸۵۲ھ) صاحب فتح الباری کی وفات سے تقریبا نصف صدی کے بعد پیدا ہوئے ہیں۔ آپ کی ذات سے بھی حافظ ابن حجر کی طرح امت کو بہت فیض پہنچا ہے۔ آپ کا فتاوی کبری جو فتاوی ہیتمیہ سے بھی مشہور ہے چار جلدوں میں مطبوعہ ہے آپ کثیر التصانیف ہیں اور آپ کی بہت کی تصانیف مطبوعہ ہیں
Shaykh al-Islam Shihab al-Din Ahmad bin Muhammad bin 'Ali, 'Allamah Ibn Hajar al-Haytami (may Allah have mercy on him) (died ... 973 AH) are a great Shafi'i jurist. His birth was in Egypt in a locality called Abu al-Haytam, hence he became famous as al-Haytami. His death was in Mecca, so he is also called al-Makki. He was born about half a century after the death of Hafiz Ibn Hajar al-Asqalani (773-852 AH), the author of Fath al-Bari. His person also brought much benefit to the Ummah, like Hafiz Ibn Hajar. His Fatawa Kubra, also known as Fatawa Haytamiyah, is printed in four volumes. He has many compositions, and many of his works are published.
Source pages p. 144

Commentary
This biography introduces the renowned Shafi'i jurist Ibn Hajar al-Haytami. Despite being a Shafi'i scholar, he is included here because his fatwa collection is widely used in fatwa practice across schools. He lived in Mecca and authored many works, including the famous four-volume Fatawa Kubra. The text notes he was born roughly fifty years after the death of the earlier scholar and hadith commentator Ibn Hajar al-Asqalani (with whom he is often confused).

Key Terms
فتاوی کبری (Fatawa Kubra): The major fatwa collection of Ibn Hajar al-Haytami, also known as Fatawa Haytamiyah.
ابن حجر ہیتمی (Ibn Hajar al-Haytami): Shafi'i jurist (d. 973 AH) known for his fatwa collection Fatawa Kubra.

Ibn al-Salah: A Bridge Scholar for Ifta' Literature
Brief biography of Ibn al-Salah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the contributions of Ibn al-Salah to hadith methodology and mufti etiquette, and explain why his treatise on adab al-mufti is relevant to Hanafi ifta'.

Core Idea
Ibn al-Salah’s Muqaddimah and Adab al-Mufti are cross-madhhab classics in hadith and ifta' methodology.

The Hanafi school, like all madhahib, has a rich tradition of ifta' literature. However, scholars from other schools have also shaped this field. Ibn al-Salah, a Shafi'i jurist and hadith master, authored two works that are studied and referenced by Hanafi muftis: his Muqaddimah in hadith sciences and his treatise on the etiquette of the mufti and the seeker of fatwa. This lesson introduces his biography and explains why these works matter in a Hanafi context.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scholar
Read the biography to note Ibn al-Salah's full name, school (Shafi'i), and his dual expertise in fiqh and hadith.
Full name: Abu Amr Uthman ibn Abd al-Rahman ibn al-Salah.
2
Recognize his major works
Two key works are mentioned: Muqaddimah Ibn al-Salah (hadith methodology) and Adab al-Mufti wa al-Mustafti (etiquette of fatwa). Note that both are used across madhahib.
The Muqaddimah is a foundational text in mustalah al-hadith, and Adab al-Mufti is a key reference in ifta' literature.
3
Connect to Hanafi ifta'
Although Ibn al-Salah is Shafi'i, his Adab al-Mufti is cited in later Hanafi works on fatwa methodology (e.g., Rasm al-Mufti). Hanafi muftis benefit from his principles on mufti conduct.
Hanafi scholars like Ibn Abidin reference cross-madhhab works when they align with Hanafi principles.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
علامہ ابو عمرو بن الصلاح عثمان بن عبدالرحمن رحمہ اللہ ( وی ۵۷ه فر ۱۳۳ ) ہور شافعی فقیہ اور بڑے محدث ہیں۔ اصول حدیث میں آپ کی کتاب مقدمہ ابن الصلاح داخل درس ہے۔ آپ کے فتاویٰ مطبوعہ ہیں اور آپ کا رسالہ ادب ہمفتی و امستفتی نایاب ہے۔
Allamah Abu 'Amr bin al-Salah 'Uthman bin 'Abd al-Rahman (may Allah have mercy on him) (born? died? 643 AH?) are a Shafi'i jurist and great hadith scholar. In hadith methodology, his book 'Muqaddimah Ibn al-Salah' is part of the curriculum. His fatawa are printed, and his treatise 'Adab al-Mufti wa al-Mustafti' is rare.
Source pages p. 144

Commentary
This biography notes Ibn al-Salah, a prominent Shafi'i jurist and hadith specialist. His Muqaddimah (Introduction to the Science of Hadith) is a classic text studied in Islamic seminaries. He also wrote fatawa and a treatise on the etiquette of the mufti and the one seeking fatwa (Adab al-Mufti wa al-Mustafti), which is now rare. This treatise is relevant to the field of ifta' and is referenced in Hanafi works as well.

Key Terms
مقدمہ ابن الصلاح (Muqaddimah Ibn al-Salah): A foundational work in hadith methodology (mustalah al-hadith) by Ibn al-Salah.
ادب المفتي والمستفتي (Adab al-Mufti wa al-Mustafti): A treatise on the ethical conduct of the mufti and the one asking for a fatwa.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway

Biography of al-Baji and Its Relevance to Hanafi Fatwa Practice
Biographical note on a Maliki scholar in a Hanafi fatwa text.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the basic biographical details of al-Baji and explain why a Maliki jurist is referenced in Hanafi fatwa literature.

Core Idea

Sadr al-Shari'ah al-Asghar: The Author of Wiqayah
Biographical notes on a Hanafi scholar and his family's works.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key Hanafi texts (Wiqayah and Naqayah) and their authors, and explain the significance of this scholarly lineage for the transmission of Hanafi fiqh.

Core Idea
The Wiqayah and its abridgment Naqayah are foundational; knowing their authors connects you to the chain of transmission.

This lesson introduces you to Sadr al-Shari'ah al-Asghar, the renowned Hanafi jurist who authored Wiqayah al-Riwayah. We will also explore his grandson's abridgment, Naqayah, and the key commentaries that followed. Understanding this scholarly family helps you appreciate the silsila (chain) of Hanafi legal scholarship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the main figure and his work
Read the passage to find the name of the primary scholar and his most famous text. Sadr al-Shari'ah al-Asghar authored Wiqayah.
Wiqayah is a standard matn in Hanafi fiqh.
2
Identify the grandson's contribution
Look for mention of a grandson who abridged Wiqayah. The result is Naqayah, an excellent summary.
Naqayah means 'choice extract'.
3
Locate the commentaries
Note the scholars who wrote commentaries on Naqayah: Qahistani (Jami' al-Rumuz) and Mulla 'Ali Qari (Sharh al-Naqayah).
Jami' al-Rumuz is a well-known printed commentary.
4
Trace the family lineage
Find the lineage: back to the companion 'Ubada ibn al-Samit, with the nisbah 'Mahbubi' from his grandson Mahbub.
This lineage adds to the scholarly authority.
5
Note the death date
The passage states Sadr al-Shari'ah al-Asghar died in the sixth century. Confirm this is approximately 6th century Hijri (though historical records often place him in the 8th).
Be aware of possible discrepancy; verify with other sources.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
شروع رسم السلتي نام سے مشہور ہے نیز پوتے نے وقایہ کا اختصار بھی کیا ہے جو نقایہ (عمدہ خلاصہ ) کہلاتا ہے اس کی شرح قہستانی نے جامع الرموز لکھی ہے جو مطبوعہ ہے (۲۹) ملاعلی قاری رحمہ اللہ نے بھی اس کی شرح لکھی ہے جو شرح نقایہ کے نام سے طبع ہوئی ہے۔ اس خاندان کا نسب حضرت عبادہ رضی اللہ عنہ سے ملتا ہے حضرت عبادہ کے پوتے کا نام محبوب تھا محبوبی اس کی طرف نسبت ہے۔ صدر الشریعۃ الاصغر کی وفات سے چھ میں ہوئی ہے۔
Beginning of the section on the conduct of the mufti. It is well-known by name; also, the grandson abbreviated the Wiqayah, which is called Naqayah (excellent summary). Its commentary by Qahistani, Jami' al-Rumuz, is printed. Mulla 'Ali Qari also wrote a commentary, published as Sharh al-Naqayah. The death of Sadr al-Shari'ah al-Asghar occurred in the sixth (century).

Commentary
This lesson provides a brief biography of the Hanafi jurist Sadr al-Shari'ah al-Asghar and his scholarly family. The passage also notes the approximate death date of Sadr al-Shari'ah al-Asghar (the younger) in the sixth century Hijri. This work is foundational in the Hanafi madhhab, and understanding its authors is important for grasping the chain of transmission (silsila) of Hanafi fiqh texts.

Key Terms

وقایہ (Wiqayah): A well-known Hanafi fiqh text by Sadr al-Shari'ah.
نقایہ (Naqayah): An abridgement of Wiqayah by the grandson of Sadr al-Shari'ah.

Ibn Hajar al-Haytami: A Shafi'i Jurist and His Fatwa Legacy
Biographical entry of Ibn Hajar al-Haytami

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key biographical facts of Ibn Hajar al-Haytami and explain the significance of his Fatawa Kubra for comparative fiqh between Hanafi and Shafi'i schools.

Core Idea
Ibn Hajar al-Haytami’s Fatawa Kubra is a major Shafi'i fatwa collection referenced across madhhabs.

This lesson introduces Shaykh al-Islam Ibn Hajar al-Haytami, a giant of the Shafi'i school whose fatawa are still consulted today. Although a Shafi'i, his work is often cited in Hanafi circles when comparing rulings. Understanding his place in the scholarly tradition helps muftis navigate cross-madhhab references and appreciate the richness of Islamic legal heritage.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scholar's full name and death year
Read the passage and note the full name 'Shihab al-Din Ahmad ibn Muhammad ibn 'Ali' and his death year 973 AH (circa 1566 CE). This distinguishes him from other scholars with similar names.
The text mentions 'al-Haytami' and 'al-Makki' as nisbas.
2
Note his birth and death locations
He was born in Egypt in a district called Abu Hiatam, hence 'al-Haytami'. He died in Makkah, hence 'al-Makki'. This shows his geographical link to both regions.
Birthplace and death place often influence a scholar's nisbah.
3
Recognize his major work: Fatawa Kubra
His most famous work is 'Fatawa Kubra', also known as 'Fatawa Haytamiyyah', in four volumes. It is a key Shafi'i fatwa collection.
The text says it is printed in four volumes.
4
Distinguish him from Ibn Hajar al-'Asqalani
Ibn Hajar al-Haytami lived about half a century after Hafiz Ibn Hajar al-'Asqalani (d. 852 AH), the famous commentator of Sahih al-Bukhari. Both are giants but from different periods and schools: 'Asqalani (Shafi'i) and al-Haytami (Shafi'i) are often confused.
Both have 'Ibn Hajar' in their name but lived in different centuries.
5
Understand his relevance for Hanafi-Shafi'i comparative fiqh
Although a Shafi'i, his fatawa are referenced by Hanafi muftis when studying inter-madhhab differences. Knowing his works enriches comparative fiqh study.
The passage emphasizes his great benefit to the community.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
شیخ الاسلام شہاب الدین احمد بن محمد بن علی علامہ ابن حجر هیتمی اور پیشی کمکی رحمہ اللہ ( ۹ ۹ فر ۹۷۳ھ ) جلیل القدر شافعی فقیہ ہیں ۔ ولادت مصر میں ابوا ہیتم نامی محلہ میں ہوئی تھی اس لیے بیتمی سے مشہور ہوئے وفات مکہ مکرمہ میں ہوئی ہے اس لیے مکی بھی کہلاتے ہیں۔ حافظ ابن حجر عسقلانی رحمہ اللہ (۷۷۳ ف ۸۵۲ھ) صاحب فتح الباری کی وفات سے تقریبا نصف صدی کے بعد پیدا ہوئے ہیں۔ آپ کی ذات سے بھی حافظ ابن حجر کی طرح امت کو بہت فیض پہنچا ہے۔ آپ کا فتاوی کبری جو فتاوی ہیتمیہ سے بھی مشہور ہے چار جلدوں میں مطبوعہ ہے آپ کثیر التصانیف ہیں اور آپ کی بہت کی تصانیف مطبوعہ ہیں (اعلام ج ۱، ص ۲۳۴)
Shaykh al-Islam Shihab al-Din Ahmad ibn Muhammad ibn 'Ali, 'Allamah Ibn Hajar al-Haytami and [؟] al-Kamki (d. 973 AH) are great Shafi'i jurists. He was born in Egypt in a district called Abu Hiatam, so he is known as al-Haytami. He died in Makkah Mukarramah, so he is also called al-Makki. Hafiz Ibn Hajar al-'Asqalani (d. 852 AH), author of Fath al-Bari, was born about half a century before him. The community has greatly benefited from him as well. His Fatawa Kubra, also known as Fatawa Haytamiyyah, is printed in four volumes. He has many works, most of which are printed (al-A'lam vol. 1, p. 234).
Source pages p. 144

Commentary
This lesson introduces the prominent Shafi'i jurist Ibn Hajar al-Haytami. He was born in Egypt and died in Makkah, earning the title 'al-Makki'. His major collection of legal responses, Fatawa Kubra (also called Fatawa Haytamiyyah), is a key reference in the Shafi'i school. He lived about half a century after the famous Hafiz Ibn Hajar al-'Asqalani. This biographical note places him in the scholarly landscape relevant to Hanafi-Shafi'i interaction.

Key Terms
ابن حجر هیتمی (Ibn Hajar al-Haytami): A Shafi'i jurist (d. 974 AH) known for his fatwa collection.
فتاوی کبری (Fatawa Kubra): His famous collection of fatwas in four volumes.

Biographical Foundations: Imam Nawawi and Ibn Qadi 'Ajlun
Biographical entries of Shafi'i scholars related to the book al-Rawdah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two Shafi'i scholars mentioned and explain the relationship between their works, specifically al-Rawdah and its supplement Zawa'id al-Rawdah.

Core Idea
Knowing the authors and their works is essential for authenticating fatwa sources within a madhhab.

This lesson introduces two prominent Shafi'i scholars whose works form part of the mufti's library. Imam Nawawi's al-Rawdah is a classic compendium of Shafi'i fiqh, while Ibn Qadi 'Ajlun's supplementary work al-Taj fi Zawa'id al-Rawdah remains in manuscript. Understanding their roles helps a mufti evaluate the chain of authority and reliability of fatwa sources.

Guided Path
1
Identify the primary text and its author
Locate the title of the main work (al-Rawdah) and its author (Imam Nawawi). Note the author's standing in the Shafi'i madhhab.
Imam Nawawi is a major Shafi'i scholar, d. 676 AH.
2
Identify the supplementary text and its author
Find the title of the supplement (al-Taj fi Zawa'id al-Rawdah) and its author (Ibn Qadi 'Ajlun). Note that the work is in manuscript.
Ibn Qadi 'Ajlun lived in the 9th century AH.
3
Analyze the relationship between the works
Understand that Zawa'id al-Rawdah builds upon al-Rawdah, adding rulings and commentary. This reflects the development of the madhhab through later scholarship.
Supplementary works do not supersede the original; they extend it.
4
Assess the implications for fatwa sourcing
Consider how a mufti would prioritize sources: primary texts are more authoritative; supplementary manuscripts require verification of chain and content.
Manuscript status does not automatically invalidate authority, but requires caution.

And by Zawa'id al-Rawdah, it likely refers to the book 'al-Taj fi Zawa'id al-Rawdah 'ala al-Minhaj' by Ibn Qadi 'Ajlun Abu al-Fadl Muhammad ibn 'Abdullah al-Mashqi (d. Parsing a Scholar's Biography in Fatwa Texts
Biographical entry of a Maliki jurist.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to extract key biographical details of a non-Hanafi scholar from a Hanafi fatwa text and explain the relevance of such entries to usul al-ifta.

Core Idea
A mufti must know scholars of all madhhabs — biographical entries in fatwa works signal cross-madhhab reference.

This passage introduces al-Baji, a Maliki jurist, within a Hanafi usul al-ifta text. Why does a Hanafi work include a Maliki's biography? Because fatwa often requires comparing rulings across madhhabs. Learning to parse such entries is a basic skill for a mufti.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Scholar's Name and Title
Extract the full name (Abu al-Walid Sulayman ibn Khalaf al-Baji al-Qurtubi) and any honorifics ('Allamah). This tells you his status and lineage.
The nisba 'al-Qurtubi' indicates he is from Cordoba, but he was born in Baja.
2
Note the Death Date and Check Ambiguity
The text gives two possible years: 340 H or 474 H. The latter (474 H) is correct for al-Baji. This ambiguity is common in OCR or manuscript errors; a mufti must cross-check reliable sources.
In fatwa work, accurate dating helps establish a scholar's era and chain of authority.
3
Identify Madhhab and Specialty
Al-Baji is described as a Maliki faqih and muhaddith. This tells you he is an authority in both fiqh and hadith, which gives weight to his works.
Knowing the madhhab is crucial: when comparing rulings, you need to know which school the scholar represents.
4
Identify His Major Work
His famous work is al-Muntaqa, a commentary on Imam Malik's Muwatta. This is a standard Maliki reference.
In a Hanafi fatwa text, such works are cited for Maliki positions.
5
Reflect on Relevance to Hanafi Fatwa
Hanafi muftis often need to reference other schools. Including biographies like this in a fatwa manual signals that the author intends to engage with cross-madhhab material.
This shows the comparative nature of usul al-ifta — a mufti must be familiar with key works of other madhhabs.

Biography of al-Qarafi: Maliki Jurist and His Relevance to Hanafi Usul al-Ifta
Biographical entry of Maliki jurist al-Qarafi

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the full name, corrected death date, and two major works of al-Qarafi, and explain how his book al-Ahkam contributes to usul al-ifta, particularly the distinction between fatwas and judicial rulings.

Core Idea
Al-Qarafi's al-Furuq and al-Ahkam are cross-madhhab references for legal maxims and fatwa theory.

This biographical entry introduces a towering figure in Maliki usul, Imam al-Qarafi. Though Maliki, his works are frequently cited in Hanafi usul al-ifta texts. Understanding his contribution helps a mufti recognize the boundaries between a fatwa and a court ruling — a key distinction in issuing correct legal opinions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scholar
State the full name (Abu al-Abbas Ahmad ibn Uris) and corrected death date (684 H, not 183 H as in the source due to OCR error).
The source gives 183 H, which is inconsistent with known historical records; al-Qarafi died in 684 H.
2
Locate him in madhhab and field
Al-Qarafi was a Maliki jurist and a renowned usuli (expert in usul al-fiqh).
3
List major works
Anwar al-Buruq fi Anwa' al-Furuq (4 volumes, on legal distinctions) and al-Ahkam fi Tamyiz al-Fatawa 'an al-Ahkam (on distinguishing fatwas from court rulings).
Both are printed.
4
Explain relevance to Hanafi usul al-ifta
Al-Qarafi's al-Ahkam directly addresses a core concern of usul al-ifta: the difference between a non-binding fatwa and a binding judicial ruling. This work is referenced across madhhabs.
The study of al-Ahkam helps a mufti understand the limits of his authority.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
علامہ قرانی ابو العباس احمد بن اور یس رحمہ اللہ (متوفی ۱۸۳ ھ ) مشہور مالکی فقیہ اور ماہر اصولی ہیں۔ مصر میں محلہ قرافہ میں آپ کی ولادت ہوئی تھی اور مصر ہی میں وفات ہوئی ہے۔ آپ کی مشہور کتاب انوار البروق فى انواء الفروق چار جلدوں میں مطبوعہ ہے۔ آپ کی دوسرى كتاب الاحكام فى تمييز الفتاوى عن الاحكام وتصرف القاضى والامام بھی مطبوعہ ہے۔
'Allamah al-Qarani [al-Qarafi] Abu al-'Abbas Ahmad ibn [؟] Uris (d. 183 H [sic]) is a famous Maliki jurist and expert in usul. He was born in the Qarafa district of Egypt and died in Egypt. His famous book Anwar al-Buruq fi Anwa' al-Furuq is printed in four volumes. His other book, al-Ahkam fi Tamyiz al-Fatawa 'an al-Ahkam wa Tasarruf al-Qadi wa al-Imam, is also printed.
Source pages p. 145

Commentary
Al-Qarafi is one of the greatest Maliki usuli scholars. His work al-Furuq is a classic on legal maxims (qawa'id). His second book, al-Ahkam, deals with distinguishing fatwas from court rulings, which is directly relevant to usul al-ifta. Though Maliki, his works are cross-referenced in Hanafi usul discussions.

Key Terms
انوار البروق فى انواء الفروق (Anwar al-Buruq fi Anwa' al-Furuq): Al-Qarafi's work on legal distinctions (furuq).
الاحكام فى تمييز الفتاوى عن الاحكام (al-Ahkam fi Tamyiz al-Fatawa 'an al-Ahkam): Al-Qarafi's work distinguishing fatwas from judicial rulings.

Qasim ibn Qutlubugha: Hanafi Biographer and Faqih
Biographical entry of Hanafi scholar Qasim ibn Qutlubugha

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the role of biographical dictionaries (Taj al-Tarajim) in the Hanafi fatwa tradition and explain the significance of Qasim ibn Qutlubugha's works.

Core Idea
A mufti must know the hierarchy of scholars — Taj al-Tarajim preserves that chain.

This lesson introduces you to Qasim ibn Qutlubugha, a ninth-century Hanafi jurist and student of Ibn al-Humam. His biographical work Taj al-Tarajim is a key source for understanding the scholarly chain (sanad) of Hanafi fatwa. Knowing the scholars and their works is essential for a mufti to weigh opinions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scholar's time and place
Note that Qasim ibn Qutlubugha was born and died in Cairo in the 9th century AH (d. 802 H). This places him in the later classical period of Hanafi scholarship.
His death date is given as 802 H, but some sources may differ slightly.
2
Identify his teacher and scholarly lineage
He was a special student (talmidh khas) of 'Allamah Ibn al-Humam, a major Hanafi authority. This lineage gives his works additional weight in the madhhab.
Ibn al-Humam (d. 861 H) is a key reference for later Hanafi jurisprudence.
3
List his major works and their status
The passage mentions four works: Taj al-Tarajim (printed), Mujibat al-Ahkam (printed), Fatawa (manuscript), and al-Tashih wa al-Tarjih li al-Quduri (unpublished). Note which are available and which are not.
Taj al-Tarajim is specifically a biographical dictionary of Hanafi scholars.
4
Explain the relevance of biographical works for iftaa
Biographical works help a mufti identify the reliability and position of scholars in the Hanafi hierarchy. They document chains of transmission (sanad) and allow a mufti to determine the weight of different opinions (tarjih).
This is part of the 'ilm al-rijal of the madhhab.

علامہ قاسم بن قطلو بغارحمہ اللہ ( ۸۰۲یف و کدھ نویں صدی کے مشہور حنفی فقیہ اور بڑے محدث ہیں۔ ولادت و وفات قاہرہ میں ہوئی ہے۔ علامہ ابن الہام کے خاص تلمیذ ہیں اور کثیر التصانیف ہیں۔ چند یہ ہیں (۱) تاج التراجم ( علمائے احناف کے حالات میں مختصر کتاب) مطبوعہ ہے (۲) موجبات الاحکام و واقعات الایام (مطبوعہ ) (۳) فتاوی ( مخطوطه) (۴) التصحيح والتربيح للمقدوری ( غیر مطبوعہ )

He was a special student of 'Allamah Ibn al-Humam and prolific author. Some of his works: (1) Taj al-Tarajim (a concise book on the biographies of Hanafi scholars), printed. (2) Mujibat al-Ahkam wa Waqi'at al-Ayyam, printed. (3) Fatawa, manuscript. (4) al-Tashih wa al-Tarjih li al-Quduri, unpublished.
Source pages p. 145

Commentary
Qasim ibn Qutlubugha is a key Hanafi scholar of the late medieval period. He was a student of Ibn al-Humam, a major authority. His works span biography, legal theory, and fatwas. His Taj al-Tarajim is a useful biographical dictionary of Hanafi scholars. This entry highlights the importance of transmitting the Hanafi legacy through biographical works.

Key Terms

Parsing a Biographical Entry: Ibn Sayyid al-Nas and His Works
Biographical entry of Shafi'i scholar Ibn Sayyid al-Nas.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to extract key biographical details from a biography entry and explain their relevance to assessing source authority in fatwa.

Core Idea
A mufti must know the madhhab and works of cited scholars to assess authority.

This lesson examines a biographical entry about the Shafi'i scholar Ibn Sayyid al-Nas. While the entry appears in a Hanafi text, it acknowledges the value of cross-madhhab scholarship. Understanding such entries trains a mufti in identifying sources and their reliability.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scholar's full name and madhhab
Extract the scholar's name: 'Allamah Ibn Sayyid al-Nas al-'Umari Abu al-Fath Muhammad ibn Muhammad. Note his madhhab is Shafi'i (mentioned as 'Shafi'i jurist').
The name includes lineage details; 'Sayyid al-Nas' is a grandfather's name.
2
Determine his geographical origins and timeline
Note his original home is Seville (Andalusia), but he was born and died in Cairo. He died in 734 AH (eighth century).
Understanding geography helps trace scholarly influences.
3
List his major works and their status
'Uyun al-Athar (printed, two volumes) is his famous sirah work. An abridgment, Nur al-'Uyun, is also printed. His commentary on Tirmidhi, al-Nafh al-Shadhi, is incomplete and unpublished.
Works with printed editions are more accessible and authoritative for fatwa.
4
Assess the authority level of each work
'Uyun al-Athar is widely known and used across madhhabs. The Tirmidhi commentary is incomplete and unpublished, thus not a primary source for hadith commentary.
A mufti should rely on complete, published works unless a manuscript is verified.
5
Understand the entry's purpose in a Hanafi text
The inclusion shows that a Hanafi mufti may reference scholars from other madhhabs in fields like sirah and hadith, which are common heritage.
This reflects the principle that knowledge is shared across madhhabs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
علامه ابن سید الناس عمری ابو الفتح محمد بن محمد رحمہ اللہ ( والحروف ۷۳۴ھ) آٹھویں صدی کے بڑے محدث اور شافعی فقیہ ہیں۔ سید الناس آپ کے سلسلہ نسب میں کسی دادا کا نام ہے۔ اصل وطن اشبیلیہ ہے مگر ولادت اور وفات قاہرہ میں ہوئی ہے۔ سیرت میں آپ کی مشہور کتاب عیون الاثر فى فنون المغازى والشمائل والسیر دو جلدوں میں مطبوعہ ہے نیز اس کا اختصار نور العیون بھی مطبوعہ ہے اور ترندی شریف کی شرح النفح الشذی نامکمل اور غیر مطبوعہ ہے۔
'Allamah Ibn Sayyid al-Nas al-'Umari Abu al-Fath Muhammad ibn Muhammad (d. [؟] 734 H) is a great hadith scholar and Shafi'i jurist of the eighth century. 'Sayyid al-Nas' is the name of some grandfather in his lineage. His original home is Seville, but he was born and died in Cairo. His famous work on the Prophet's biography is 'Uyun al-Athar fi Funun al-Maghazi wa al-Shama'il wa al-Siyar, printed in two volumes. Also an abridgment, Nur al-'Uyun, is printed. His commentary on Tirmidhi titled al-Nafh al-Shadhi is incomplete and unpublished.
Source pages p. 145

Commentary
Ibn Sayyid al-Nas is recognized for his contributions to sirah (Prophetic biography). His 'Uyun al-Athar is a standard work in the field. He also worked on hadith commentary, though his commentary on Tirmidhi remains incomplete. This entry, again from a Hanafi text, shows that the knowledge of scholars from other madhhabs is integral to the broader Islamic scholarly tradition.

Key Terms
عیون الاثر ('Uyun al-Athar): Ibn Sayyid al-Nas's work on the Prophet's biography.
النفح الشذی (al-Nafh al-Shadhi): Ibn Sayyid al-Nas's incomplete commentary on Jami' al-Tirmidhi.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Ibn Kamal Pasha: A Prolific Hanafi Scholar
Biographical entry of Hanafi scholar Ibn Kamal Pasha

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key contributions of Ibn Kamal Pasha to Hanafi scholarship and list his major unpublished works.

Core Idea
One scholar, almost all sciences: Ibn Kamal Pasha authored works in virtually every Islamic discipline.

This biography of Ibn Kamal Pasha (d. 940/1534) illuminates the vast scholarly output of an Ottoman Hanafi jurist and traditionist. Although only a fraction of his works are printed, his biographers note that he authored something in every field of knowledge. This lesson highlights his importance in the Hanafi tradition and the loss of much of his legacy.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scholar's full name and death date
Read the first line of the Arabic text. Note the full name: Qadi Shams al-Din Ahmad ibn Sulayman ibn Kamal Pasha. The death date is given as '93' (probably 930 H).
The death date is uncertain; some sources say 940 H.
2
Understand the biographers' claim
The text says 'there is almost no science in which Ibn Kamal Pasha has not authored a work.' This indicates his encyclopedic range across Islamic sciences.
3
List the unpublished works mentioned
The text lists four unpublished works: (1) Tabaqat al-Fuqaha', (2) Tabaqat al-Mujtahidin, (3) al-Islah wa al-Idah, (4) Taghyir al-Tanqih. Note that only a collection of 36 short treatises is printed.
These works cover fiqh, usul, and biographical classifications.

قاضی شمس الدین احمد بن سلیمان بن کمال پاشا رحمہ اللہ (متوفی ۹۳ ) مشہور حنفی فقیه محدث اور کثیر التصانیف عالم ہیں۔ آپ کے سوانح نگاروں نے لکھا ہے کہ فلما یو فن من الفنون وليس لابن کمال پاشا مصنف فيه ( اعلام ) مگر مطبوعہ صرف چند رسائل کا مجموعہ ہے جس میں چھوٹے چھوٹے ۳۶ رسالے ہیں اور غیر مطبوعہ کتابوں میں سے چند یہ بين (۱) طبقات الفقهاء (۲) طبقات المجتهدين (۳) الاصلاح والايضاح (فقه حنفی میں متن اور شرح ) (۴) تغییر التنقیح (اصول فقہ کا متن ہے پھر خود ہی اس کی شرح لکھی
Qadi Shams al-Din Ahmad ibn Sulayman ibn Kamal Pasha (d. 93? H) is a famous Hanafi jurist, hadith scholar, and prolific author. Among his unpublished works are: (1) Tabaqat al-Fuqaha', (2) Tabaqat al-Mujtahidin, (3) al-Islah wa al-Idah (a text and commentary in Hanafi fiqh), (4) Taghyir al-Tanqih (a text on usul al-fiqh with his own commentary).
Source pages p. 145

Commentary
Ibn Kamal Pasha (also known as Kamal Pashazade) was an Ottoman Hanafi scholar of vast erudition. He wrote on almost every Islamic science. Unfortunately, only a fraction of his works, a collection of 36 short treatises, have been printed. His unpublished works include important texts on the classes of jurists and mujtahids, as well as contributions to Hanafi fiqh and usul al-fiqh. This entry emphasizes his encyclopedic knowledge and the loss of many of his writings.

Key Terms
ابن کمال پاشا (Ibn Kamal Pasha): An Ottoman Hanafi scholar (d. 940 H) known for his vast writings.

Key Terms from Source Passage

The Four Imams and Founders of the Hanafi School
Biographical sketch of core Hanafi authorities.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the four Sunni Imams and the two primary students of Abu Hanifa, and state their key contributions to Hanafi fiqh and ifta.

Core Idea
The Hanafi school rests on the authority of Abu Hanifa, transmitted through Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani.

This passage introduces the foundational figures whose rulings and works form the basis of Hanafi fatwa. Understanding their hierarchy is essential for a mufti, as it determines which opinions are relied upon in legal verdicts.

Guided Path
1
Locate the listing of the four Imams
In the Arabic text, find the line that begins with 'ائِمَّةُ أَرْبَعَة' (four Imams). Note their names, birth/death years, and order.
The four Imams are listed in chronological order: Abu Hanifa, Malik, Shafi'i, and Ahmad ibn Hanbal.
2
Identify the two chief students of Abu Hanifa
After the Imams, the text describes Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani. Note their relationship to Abu Hanifa and their roles as qadi and compiler.
Abu Yusuf was the first to hold the title 'Qadi al-Qudat' and authored Kitab al-Kharaj.
3
List their key printed works
Read the entries for Abu Yusuf and Muhammad and list the printed books mentioned for each. Recognize these as core Zahir al-Riwayah texts.
Muhammad's works include al-Asl (al-Mabsut), Jami' Kabir, Jami' Saghir, and al-Hujjah 'ala Ahl al-Madinah.
4
Understand the hierarchy for fatwa
Reflect on why these figures are included in a work on ifta methodology. Their works form the primary source for Hanafi rulings, and knowing their positions helps a mufti weigh opinions.
The ranking: Abu Hanifa, then Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, then later scholars.

علامہ قرانی ابو العباس احمد بن ادریس رحمہ اللہ (متوفی ۱۸۳ ھ ) مشہور مالکی فقیہ اور ماہر اصولی ہیں۔ مصر میں محلہ قرافہ میں آپ کی ولادت ہوئی تھی اور مصر ہی میں وفات ہوئی ہے۔ آپ کی مشہور کتاب انوار البروق فی انواء الفروق چار جلدوں میں مطبوعہ ہے۔ آپ کی دوسرى كتاب الاحكام فی تمييز الفتاوى عن الاحكام وتصرف القاضى والامام بھی مطبوعہ ہے۔
-11
علامہ قاسم بن قطلوبغا رحمہ اللہ ( ۸۰۲ ھ) نویں صدی کے مشہور حنفی فقیہ اور بڑے محدث ہیں۔ ولادت و وفات قاہرہ میں ہوئی ہے۔ علامہ ابن الہام کے خاص تلمیذ ہیں اور کثیر التصانیف ہیں۔ چند یہ ہیں (۱) تاج التراجم ( علمائے احناف کے حالات میں مختصر کتاب) مطبوعہ ہے (۲) موجبات الاحکام و واقعات الایام (مطبوعہ ) (۳) فتاوی ( مخطوطه) (۴) التصحيح والتربيح للمقدوری ( غیر مطبوعہ ) علامه ابن سید الناس عمری ابو الفتح محمد بن محمد رحمہ اللہ ( المتوفى ۷۳۴ھ) آٹھویں صدی کے بڑے محدث اور شافعی فقیہ ہیں۔ سید الناس آپ کے سلسلہ نسب میں کسی دادا کا نام ہے۔ اصل وطن اشبیلیہ ہے مگر ولادت اور وفات قاہرہ میں ہوئی ہے۔ سیرت میں آپ کی مشہور کتاب عیون الاثر فی فنون المغازى والشمائل والسیر دو جلدوں میں مطبوعہ ہے نیز اس کا اختصار نور العیون بھی مطبوعہ ہے اور ترندی شریف کی شرح النفح الشذی نامکمل اور غیر مطبوعہ ہے۔ قاضی شمس الدین احمد بن سلیمان بن کمال پاشا رحمہ اللہ (متوفی ۹۳۰ ھ) مشہور حنفی فقیہ محدث اور کثیر التصانیف عالم ہیں۔ آپ کے سوانح نگاروں نے لکھا ہے کہ فلما یو فن من الفنون وليس لابن کمال پاشا مصنف فيه ( اعلام ) مگر مطبوعہ صرف چند رسائل کا مجموعہ ہے جس میں چھوٹے چھوٹے ۳۶ رسالے ہیں اور غیر مطبوعہ کتابوں میں سے چند یہ بین (۱) طبقات الفقهاء (۲) طبقات المجتهدين (۳) الاصلاح والايضاح (فقه حنفی میں متن اور شرح ) (۴) تغییر التنقیح (اصول فقہ کا متن ہے پھر خود ہی اس کی شرح لکھی ہے ) (۵) ہدایہ کا حاشیہ آپ ابن کمال اور ابن الکمال سے مشہور ہیں ۔ ائمہ اربعہ یہ ہیں (۱) امام اعظم ابو حنیفہ نعمان بن ثابت کوفی رحمہ اللہ ولادت ۸۰ وفات ۱۵۰ (۲) امام مالک بن انس مدنی رحمہ اللہ ولادت ۹۳ ھ وفات ۱۷۹ (۳) امام محمد بن ادریس شافعی ہاشمی رحمہ اللہ ولادت ۱۵۰ ھ وفات ۲۰۴ (۴) امام احمد بن محمد بن حنبل بغدادی رحمہ اللہ ولادت ۱۶۴ ھ وفات ۲۴۱ھ۔
-۱۴
امام ابو یوسف یعقوب بن ابراہیم انصاری کوفی بغدادی رحمہ اللہ ( ۱۳۱ ف ۱۸۲ ھ ) امام اعظم کے سب سے بڑے شاگرد اور امام محمد کے استاذ ہیں ۔ عباسی خلفاء مہدی اور ہارون رشید کے زمانہ میں قاضی رہے۔ قاضی القضاۃ کا خطاب سب سے پہلے آپ کو دیا گیا۔ آپ کی مطبوعہ کتابیں یہ ہیں (۱) کتاب الخراج (۲) کتاب الآثار (۳) کتاب الرد علی سیر الاوزاعی غیر مطبوعہ کتابیں متعدد ہیں جیسے مبسوط امالی وغیرہ۔ امام ابو عبد الله محمد بن الحسن شیبانی رحمہ اللہ ( ۱۳۲ ف ۱۸۹ھ) امام اعظم کے خاص تلمیذ اور ان کے علوم کے جامع اور ناشر ہیں۔ امام اعظم کی وفات کے بعد امام ابو یوسف سے تعلیم مکمل کی آپ کی مطبوعہ کتابیں یہ ہیں (1) کتاب الاصل ( مبسوط ) (۲) جامع کبیر (۳) جامع صغیر (۴) زیادات (۵) زیادات الزيادات (۶) کتاب الآثار (۷) شرح السير الكبير للمرضى اصل کتاب طبع نہیں ہوئی) (۸) کتاب الحجہ علی اہل المدینه (۹) موطا محمد (۱۰) کتاب الا مالی ۔ غیر مطبوعہ کتا بیں بھی متعدد ہیں۔
-۱۵
امام ابو بکر خصاف (موچی ) احمد بن عمر شیبانی رحمہ اللہ (متوفی ۲۶۱) جلیل القدر حنفی فقیہ ہیں قاضی خان فرماتے ہیں والخصاف كان كبيراً في العلم، يجوز الاقتداء به (شامی ج ۲ ص ۲۹۵) آپ کی دو کتابیں مطبوعہ ہیں ایک احکام الاوقاف دوسری کتاب الحیل اور ادب القاضی مخطوطہ ہے باقی کتا میں مفقود ہیں۔ امام ابو جعفر احمد بن محمد بن سلامه از دی طحاوی رحمہ اللہ ( ۲۳۹ ف ۳۲۱ ھ ) مشہور حنفی فقیہ اور بڑے محدث ہیں۔ مصر کے طحا مقام میں پیدا ہوئے ۔ امام شافعی کے تلمیذ رشید امام مزنی رحمہ اللہ کے بھانجے تھے آپ کی مطبوعہ کتابیں یہ ہیں (۱) شرح معانی الآثار (طحاوی شریف) (۲) بیان مشکل الآثار (اس کتاب کا چوتھائی حصہ پانچ جلدوں میں طبع ہوا
Beginning of Rasm al-Mufti. Maliki jurist and hadith scholar. Place of birth is Baja in Andalusia, and death occurred in Al-Mariyya. His famous book is the commentary on Muwatta Imam Malik, al-Muntaqa, printed.
-9
Allamah Qarafi Abu al-Abbas Ahmad ibn Idris (d. 683 AH), famous Maliki jurist and usuli scholar. He was born in Egypt in the district of Qarafa and died in Egypt. His famous book Anwar al-Buruq fi Anwa al-Furuq is printed in four volumes. His other book al-Ahkam fi Tamyiz al-Fatawa an al-Ahkam wa Tasarruf al-Qadi wa al-Imam is also printed.
-11
Allamah Qasim ibn Qutlubugha (d. 802 AH), famous Hanafi jurist and great hadith scholar of the ninth century. Birth and death in Cairo. He was a special student of Allamah Ibn al-Humam and prolific author. Among his works: (1) Taj al-Tarajim (a brief book on biographies of Hanafi scholars) printed, (2) Mujibat al-Ahkam wa Waqi'at al-Ayyam (printed), (3) Fatawa (manuscript), (4) al-Tashih wa al-Tarjih li al-Maqduri (unprinted). Allamah Ibn Sayyid al-Nas al-Amri Abu al-Fath Muhammad ibn Muhammad (d. 734 AH), great hadith scholar and Shafi'i jurist of the eighth century. 'Sayyid al-Nas' is the name of one of his grandfathers. His original homeland is Seville, but birth and death in Cairo. His famous work on Seerah is 'Uyun al-Athar fi Funun al-Maghazi wa al-Shama'il wa al-Siyar in two volumes printed; also its abridgment Nur al-'Uyun is printed, and his commentary on Tirmidhi, al-Nafh al-Shadhi, is incomplete and unprinted. Qadi Shams al-Din Ahmad ibn Sulayman ibn Kamal Pasha (d. 930 AH), famous Hanafi jurist, hadith scholar, and prolific author. His biographers have written that 'there is no art in which Ibn Kamal Pasha does not have a composition' (A'lam), but only a collection of 36 small treatises is printed. Among his unprinted books: (1) Tabaqat al-Fuqaha, (2) Tabaqat al-Mujtahidin, (3) al-Islah wa al-Idah (text and commentary in Hanafi fiqh), (4) Taghyir al-Tanqih (a text in usul al-fiqh, then he wrote a commentary on it), (5) a gloss on Hidayah. He is known as Ibn Kamal and Ibn al-Kamal. The four Imams are: (1) Imam A'zam Abu Hanifa Nu'man ibn Thabit Kufi (d. 80/150), (2) Imam Malik ibn Anas Madani (d. 93/179), (3) Imam Muhammad ibn Idris Shafi'i Hashimi (d. 150/204), (4) Imam Ahmad ibn Muhammad ibn Hanbal Baghdadi (d. 164/241).
-14
Imam Abu Yusuf Ya'qub ibn Ibrahim Ansari Kufi Baghdadi (d. 131/182) is the greatest student of Imam A'zam and teacher of Imam Muhammad. He served as qadi during the caliphates of al-Mahdi and Harun al-Rashid. He was the first to be given the title Qadi al-Qudat. His printed books include: (1) Kitab al-Kharaj, (2) Kitab al-Athar, (3) Kitab al-Radd 'ala Siyar al-Awza'i. He has many unprinted books such as al-Mabsut, Amali, etc. Imam Abu Abdullah Muhammad ibn al-Hasan al-Shaybani (d. 132/189) is a special student of Imam A'zam and the compiler and publisher of his knowledge. After the death of Imam A'zam, he completed his studies under Imam Abu Yusuf. His printed books include: (1) Kitab al-Asl (al-Mabsut), (2) Jami' Kabir, (3) Jami' Saghir, (4) Ziyadat, (5) Ziyadat al-Ziyadat, (6) Kitab al-Athar, (7) Sharh al-Siyar al-Kabir li al-Mardini (the original book not printed), (8) Kitab al-Hujjah 'ala Ahl al-Madinah, (9) Muwatta Muhammad, (10) Kitab al-Amali. He also has many unprinted books.
-15
Imam Abu Bakr al-Khassaf (al-Mawchi) Ahmad ibn Umar al-Shaybani (d. 261), a great Hanafi jurist. Qadi Khan said: 'Al-Khassaf was great in knowledge; it is permissible to follow him' (Shami, vol. 2, p. 295). Two of his books are printed: Ahkam al-Awqaf and Kitab al-Hiyal; Adab al-Qadi is a manuscript; the rest of his books are lost. Imam Abu Ja'far Ahmad ibn Muhammad ibn Salamah al-Azdi al-Tahawi (d. 239/321), famous Hanafi jurist and great hadith scholar. Born in the town of Taha in Egypt. He was the nephew of Imam al-Muzani, the dedicated student of Imam Shafi'i. His printed books include: (1) Sharh Ma'ani al-Athar (Tahawi Sharif), (2) Bayan Mushkil al-Athar (a quarter of this book printed in five volumes).
Source pages p. 145

Commentary
This passage is a biographical section from the commentary on Rasm al-Mufti, introducing key scholars whose works and positions are foundational for Hanafi ifta methodology. It begins with a Maliki scholar, then al-Qarafi (Maliki usuli), then Qasim ibn Qutlubugha (Hanafi historian and jurist), Ibn Sayyid al-Nas (Shafi'i), and Ibn Kamal Pasha (Hanafi). It then lists the four major Imams and proceeds to the direct students of Abu Hanifa: Abu Yusuf, Muhammad al-Shaybani, and later Hanafi scholars al-Khassaf and al-Tahawi. Each entry provides birth/death dates, key works, and their standing in the tradition. For the Hanafi mufti, these biographies establish the chain of authority and the sources from which rulings are derived. The mention of al-Khassaf's Kitab al-Hiyal and al-Tahawi's works on hadith and fiqh indicates the depth of the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
رسم المفتي (Rasm al-Mufti): A work on the rules and conditions for issuing fatwas in the Hanafi tradition.
فقيه (faqīh): A scholar qualified to derive legal rulings from detailed evidence.
محدث (muḥaddith): A scholar specializing in hadith narration and criticism.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Who was the first scholar to hold the title 'Qadi al-Qudat'?
A) Imam Abu Hanifa
B) Imam Abu Yusuf
C) Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani
D) Imam al-Tahawi

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school's authority flows from Abu Hanifa through Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, whose works remain primary for fatwa.

Life of the Author
intermediate
8 min
Later Authorities in Hanafi Fatwa Methodology
Biographical sketches of later scholars relevant to Hanafi ifta.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify later Hanafi scholars (Qasim ibn Qutlubugha, Ibn Kamal Pasha, al-Khassaf, al-Tahawi) and non-Hanafi scholars mentioned in Rasm al-Mufti, and state their key works and relevance for fatwa.

Core Idea
Later Hanafi scholars enriched the madhhab with critical works on hadith, legal stratagems, and fatwa methodology.

This passage continues with biographical entries of scholars who built upon the foundation laid by the early Hanafi masters. These include historians, commentators, and experts in legal stratagems. Understanding their contributions helps a mufti navigate the later fatwa literature and appreciate cross-madhhab references.

Guided Path
1
Identify the non-Hanafi scholars mentioned
Find the entries for al-Qarafi (Maliki usuli) and Ibn Sayyid al-Nas (Shafi'i muhaddith). Note their works and why a Hanafi text includes them.
These scholars are referenced for methodological comparison or because their works are used across madhhabs.
2
Locate the Hanafi scholars Qasim ibn Qutlubugha and Ibn Kamal Pasha
Read their entries. Note their importance as historians of the Hanafi school and commentators.
Ibn Qutlubugha wrote Taj al-Tarajim (biographies) and Mujibat al-Ahkam. Ibn Kamal Pasha wrote glosses on Hidayah and works in usul.
3
Examine al-Khassaf and al-Tahawi
Al-Khassaf is known for Kitab al-Hiyal and Ahkam al-Awqaf. Al-Tahawi for Sharh Ma'ani al-Athar. Note their expertise in hadith and legal theory.
Al-Tahawi bridges hadith and fiqh, while al-Khassaf's works address legal stratagems permissible in Hanafi law.
4
Understand their relevance for ifta
These scholars' works are referenced in fatwa compilations and commentaries. A mufti must know when to rely on them versus the core texts.
Al-Tahawi's works are particularly important for hadith-based rulings; al-Khassaf for issues of waqf and legal stratagems.

علامہ قاسم بن قطلوبغا رحمہ اللہ ( ۸۰۲ ھ) نویں صدی کے مشہور حنفی فقیہ اور بڑے محدث ہیں۔ ولادت و وفات قاہرہ میں ہوئی ہے۔ علامہ ابن الہام کے خاص تلمیذ ہیں اور کثیر التصانیف ہیں۔ چند یہ ہیں (۱) تاج التراجم ( علمائے احناف کے حالات میں مختصر کتاب) مطبوعہ ہے (۲) موجبات الاحکام و واقعات الایام (مطبوعہ ) (۳) فتاوی ( مخطوطه) (۴) التصحيح والتربيح للمقدوری ( غیر مطبوعہ ) علامه ابن سید الناس عمری ابو الفتح محمد بن محمد رحمہ اللہ ( المتوفى ۷۳۴ھ) آٹھویں صدی کے بڑے محدث اور شافعی فقیہ ہیں۔ سید الناس آپ کے سلسلہ نسب میں کسی دادا کا نام ہے۔ اصل وطن اشبیلیہ ہے مگر ولادت اور وفات قاہرہ میں ہوئی ہے۔ سیرت میں آپ کی مشہور کتاب عیون الاثر فی فنون المغازى والشمائل والسیر دو جلدوں میں مطبوعہ ہے نیز اس کا اختصار نور العیون بھی مطبوعہ ہے اور ترندی شریف کی شرح النفح الشذی نامکمل اور غیر مطبوعہ ہے۔ قاضی شمس الدین احمد بن سلیمان بن کمال پاشا رحمہ اللہ (متوفی ۹۳۰ ھ) مشہور حنفی فقیہ محدث اور کثیر التصانیف عالم ہیں۔ آپ کے سوانح نگاروں نے لکھا ہے کہ فلما یو فن من الفنون وليس لابن کمال پاشا مصنف فيه ( اعلام ) مگر مطبوعہ صرف چند رسائل کا مجموعہ ہے جس میں چھوٹے چھوٹے ۳۶ رسالے ہیں اور غیر مطبوعہ کتابوں میں سے چند یہ بین (۱) طبقات الفقهاء (۲) طبقات المجتهدين (۳) الاصلاح والايضاح (فقه حنفی میں متن اور شرح ) (۴) تغییر التنقیح (اصول فقہ کا متن ہے پھر خود ہی اس کی شرح لکھی ہے ) (۵) ہدایہ کا حاشیہ آپ ابن کمال اور ابن الکمال سے مشہور ہیں ۔ ائمہ اربعہ یہ ہیں (۱) امام اعظم ابو حنیفہ نعمان بن ثابت کوفی رحمہ اللہ ولادت ۸۰ وفات ۱۵۰ (۲) امام مالک بن انس مدنی رحمہ اللہ ولادت ۹۳ ھ وفات ۱۷۹ (۳) امام محمد بن ادریس شافعی ہاشمی رحمہ اللہ ولادت ۱۵۰ ھ وفات ۲۰۴ (۴) امام احمد بن محمد بن حنبل بغدادی رحمہ اللہ ولادت ۱۶۴ ھ وفات ۲۴۱ھ۔
-۱۴
امام ابو یوسف یعقوب بن ابراہیم انصاری کوفی بغدادی رحمہ اللہ ( ۱۳۱ ف ۱۸۲ ھ ) امام اعظم کے سب سے بڑے شاگرد اور امام محمد کے استاذ ہیں ۔ عباسی خلفاء مہدی اور ہارون رشید کے زمانہ میں قاضی رہے۔ قاضی القضاۃ کا خطاب سب سے پہلے آپ کو دیا گیا۔ آپ کی مطبوعہ کتابیں یہ ہیں (۱) کتاب الخراج (۲) کتاب الآثار (۳) کتاب الرد علی سیر الاوزاعی غیر مطبوعہ کتابیں متعدد ہیں جیسے مبسوط امالی وغیرہ۔ امام ابو عبد الله محمد بن الحسن شیبانی رحمہ اللہ ( ۱۳۲ ف ۱۸۹ھ) امام اعظم کے خاص تلمیذ اور ان کے علوم کے جامع اور ناشر ہیں۔ امام اعظم کی وفات کے بعد امام ابو یوسف سے تعلیم مکمل کی آپ کی مطبوعہ کتابیں یہ ہیں (1) کتاب الاصل ( مبسوط ) (۲) جامع کبیر (۳) جامع صغیر (۴) زیادات (۵) زیادات الزيادات (۶) کتاب الآثار (۷) شرح السير الكبير للمرضى اصل کتاب طبع نہیں ہوئی) (۸) کتاب الحجہ علی اہل المدینه (۹) موطا محمد (۱۰) کتاب الا مالی ۔ غیر مطبوعہ کتا بیں بھی متعدد ہیں۔
-۱۵
امام ابو بکر خصاف (موچی ) احمد بن عمر شیبانی رحمہ اللہ (متوفی ۲۶۱) جلیل القدر حنفی فقیہ ہیں قاضی خان فرماتے ہیں والخصاف كان كبيراً في العلم، يجوز الاقتداء به (شامی ج ۲ ص ۲۹۵) آپ کی دو کتابیں مطبوعہ ہیں ایک احکام الاوقاف دوسری کتاب الحیل اور ادب القاضی مخطوطہ ہے باقی کتا میں مفقود ہیں۔ امام ابو جعفر احمد بن محمد بن سلامه از دی طحاوی رحمہ اللہ ( ۲۳۹ ف ۳۲۱ ھ ) مشہور حنفی فقیہ اور بڑے محدث ہیں۔ مصر کے طحا مقام میں پیدا ہوئے ۔ امام شافعی کے تلمیذ رشید امام مزنی رحمہ اللہ کے بھانجے تھے آپ کی مطبوعہ کتابیں یہ ہیں (۱) شرح معانی الآثار (طحاوی شریف) (۲) بیان مشکل الآثار (اس کتاب کا چوتھائی حصہ پانچ جلدوں میں طبع ہوا
Beginning of Rasm al-Mufti. Maliki jurist and hadith scholar. Place of birth is Baja in Andalusia, and death occurred in Al-Mariyya. His famous book is the commentary on Muwatta Imam Malik, al-Muntaqa, printed.
-9
Allamah Qarafi Abu al-Abbas Ahmad ibn Idris (d. 683 AH), famous Maliki jurist and usuli scholar. He was born in Egypt in the district of Qarafa and died in Egypt. His famous book Anwar al-Buruq fi Anwa al-Furuq is printed in four volumes. His other book al-Ahkam fi Tamyiz al-Fatawa an al-Ahkam wa Tasarruf al-Qadi wa al-Imam is also printed.
-11
Allamah Qasim ibn Qutlubugha (d. 802 AH), famous Hanafi jurist and great hadith scholar of the ninth century. Birth and death in Cairo. He was a special student of Allamah Ibn al-Humam and prolific author. Among his works: (1) Taj al-Tarajim (a brief book on biographies of Hanafi scholars) printed, (2) Mujibat al-Ahkam wa Waqi'at al-Ayyam (printed), (3) Fatawa (manuscript), (4) al-Tashih wa al-Tarjih li al-Maqduri (unprinted). Allamah Ibn Sayyid al-Nas al-Amri Abu al-Fath Muhammad ibn Muhammad (d. 734 AH), great hadith scholar and Shafi'i jurist of the eighth century. 'Sayyid al-Nas' is the name of one of his grandfathers. His original homeland is Seville, but birth and death in Cairo. His famous work on Seerah is 'Uyun al-Athar fi Funun al-Maghazi wa al-Shama'il wa al-Siyar in two volumes printed; also its abridgment Nur al-'Uyun is printed, and his commentary on Tirmidhi, al-Nafh al-Shadhi, is incomplete and unprinted. Qadi Shams al-Din Ahmad ibn Sulayman ibn Kamal Pasha (d. 930 AH), famous Hanafi jurist, hadith scholar, and prolific author. His biographers have written that 'there is no art in which Ibn Kamal Pasha does not have a composition' (A'lam), but only a collection of 36 small treatises is printed. Among his unprinted books: (1) Tabaqat al-Fuqaha, (2) Tabaqat al-Mujtahidin, (3) al-Islah wa al-Idah (text and commentary in Hanafi fiqh), (4) Taghyir al-Tanqih (a text in usul al-fiqh, then he wrote a commentary on it), (5) a gloss on Hidayah. He is known as Ibn Kamal and Ibn al-Kamal. The four Imams are: (1) Imam A'zam Abu Hanifa Nu'man ibn Thabit Kufi (d. 80/150), (2) Imam Malik ibn Anas Madani (d. 93/179), (3) Imam Muhammad ibn Idris Shafi'i Hashimi (d. 150/204), (4) Imam Ahmad ibn Muhammad ibn Hanbal Baghdadi (d. 164/241).
-14
Imam Abu Yusuf Ya'qub ibn Ibrahim Ansari Kufi Baghdadi (d. 131/182) is the greatest student of Imam A'zam and teacher of Imam Muhammad. He served as qadi during the caliphates of al-Mahdi and Harun al-Rashid. He was the first to be given the title Qadi al-Qudat. His printed books include: (1) Kitab al-Kharaj, (2) Kitab al-Athar, (3) Kitab al-Radd 'ala Siyar al-Awza'i. He has many unprinted books such as al-Mabsut, Amali, etc. Imam Abu Abdullah Muhammad ibn al-Hasan al-Shaybani (d. 132/189) is a special student of Imam A'zam and the compiler and publisher of his knowledge. After the death of Imam A'zam, he completed his studies under Imam Abu Yusuf. His printed books include: (1) Kitab al-Asl (al-Mabsut), (2) Jami' Kabir, (3) Jami' Saghir, (4) Ziyadat, (5) Ziyadat al-Ziyadat, (6) Kitab al-Athar, (7) Sharh al-Siyar al-Kabir li al-Mardini (the original book not printed), (8) Kitab al-Hujjah 'ala Ahl al-Madinah, (9) Muwatta Muhammad, (10) Kitab al-Amali. He also has many unprinted books.
-15
Imam Abu Bakr al-Khassaf (al-Mawchi) Ahmad ibn Umar al-Shaybani (d. 261), a great Hanafi jurist. Qadi Khan said: 'Al-Khassaf was great in knowledge; it is permissible to follow him' (Shami, vol. 2, p. 295). Two of his books are printed: Ahkam al-Awqaf and Kitab al-Hiyal; Adab al-Qadi is a manuscript; the rest of his books are lost. Imam Abu Ja'far Ahmad ibn Muhammad ibn Salamah al-Azdi al-Tahawi (d. 239/321), famous Hanafi jurist and great hadith scholar. Born in the town of Taha in Egypt. He was the nephew of Imam al-Muzani, the dedicated student of Imam Shafi'i. His printed books include: (1) Sharh Ma'ani al-Athar (Tahawi Sharif), (2) Bayan Mushkil al-Athar (a quarter of this book printed in five volumes).
Source pages p. 145

Commentary
This passage is a biographical section from the commentary on Rasm al-Mufti, introducing key scholars whose works and positions are foundational for Hanafi ifta methodology. It begins with a Maliki scholar, then al-Qarafi (Maliki usuli), then Qasim ibn Qutlubugha (Hanafi historian and jurist), Ibn Sayyid al-Nas (Shafi'i), and Ibn Kamal Pasha (Hanafi). It then lists the four major Imams and proceeds to the direct students of Abu Hanifa: Abu Yusuf, Muhammad al-Shaybani, and later Hanafi scholars al-Khassaf and al-Tahawi. Each entry provides birth/death dates, key works, and their standing in the tradition. For the Hanafi mufti, these biographies establish the chain of authority and the sources from which rulings are derived. The mention of al-Khassaf's Kitab al-Hiyal and al-Tahawi's works on hadith and fiqh indicates the depth of the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
كتاب الحيل (Kitab al-Hiyal): A book on legal stratagems, i.e., permissible ways to achieve a lawful objective without violating the law.
طلحاوی شریف (Tahawi Sharif): The common name for Sharh Ma'ani al-Athar, a commentary on hadith by Imam al-Tahawi.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which later Hanafi scholar authored 'Taj al-Tarajim', a biographical work on Hanafi scholars?
A) Ibn Kamal Pasha
B) Qasim ibn Qutlubugha
C) Al-Khassaf
D) Al-Tahawi

Key Takeaway
Later Hanafi scholars like al-Khassaf, al-Tahawi, and Ibn Kamal Pasha produced essential works in waqf, hadith, and fatwa methodology that complement the core Zahir al-Riwayah texts.

Life of the Author
beginner
6 min
Key Hanafi Jurists and Their Works
Biographical survey of Hanafi jurists from Sharh Rasm al-Mufti.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the major Hanafi jurists of the classical period, state their key works, and explain their role in the Hanafi transmission chain for fatwa.

Core Idea
Knowing the chain of Hanafi scholars is essential for a mufti to correctly cite authority and weigh opinions.

This passage from Sharh Rasm al-Mufti introduces the great Hanafi jurists whose works form the backbone of Hanafi fatwa methodology. Understanding who these scholars are, their relationship to each other, and which books they authored is critical for any mufti to navigate the Hanafi textual tradition. This lesson will help you build a mental map of the Hanafi scholarly lineage.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four founding Imams
Note the names, dates, and schools of the four Sunni Imams. Focus on Imam Abu Hanifa as the source of the Hanafi school.
Memorize birth and death years as anchors.
2
Focus on Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad
These are the primary disciples (Sahibayn). Know their titles, key roles (e.g., first Qadi al-Qudat), and major published works.
Imam Muhammad compiled the six books of Zahir al-Riwayah.
3
Note the later Iraqi jurists
Al-Khassaf and al-Tahawi are important for awqaf, hiyal, and hadith-based fiqh. Al-Karkhi wrote foundational usul principles.
Al-Karkhi's Usul al-Karkhi is a key usul text.
4
Understand the fifth-century Transoxianan scholars
Al-Halwani, al-Sarakhsi, and al-Bazdawi are major figures from the eastern Hanafi tradition. Al-Sarakhsi's al-Mabsut is a comprehensive reference.
Al-Bazdawi's Usul al-Bazdawi is a core usul text.
5
Connect each scholar to a key work
For each scholar, identify one published work that is essential for fatwa. This aids in recalling the chain of authority.
Use the list provided in the passage.

آپ فتوی کیسے دیں؟ ۱۴۵ شرح رسم المفتی ہے۔ (۵) ہدایہ کا حاشیہ آپ ابن کمال اور ابن الکمال سے مشہور ہیں۔ ائمہ اربعہ یہ ہیں (۱) امام اعظم ابو حنیفہ نعمان بن ثابت کوفی رحمہ اللہ ولادت ۸۰ وفات ۱۵۰ (۲) امام مالک بن انس مدنی رحمہ اللہ ولادت ۹۳ ھ وفات ۱۷۹ (۳) امام محمد بن اوریس شافعی ہاشمی کی رحمہ اللہ ولادت ۱۵۰ ھ وفات ۵۲۰۴ (۴) امام احمد بن محمد بن حنبل بغدادی رحمہ اللہ ولادت ۱۶۴ ھ وفات ۲۴ھ۔

امام ابو یوسف یعقوب بن ابراہیم انصاری، کوئی بغدادی رحمہ اللہ (۱۳ ف (۱۸۲ ھ ) امام اعظم کے سب سے بڑے شبا گرد اور امام محمد کے استاذ ہیں۔ عباسی خلفاء مہدی بادی اور ہارون رشید کے زمانہ میں قاضی رہے۔ قاضی القضاۃ کا خطاب سب سے پہلے آپ کو دیا گیا۔ آپ کی مطبوعہ کتابیں یہ ہیں (۱) کتاب الخراج (۲) کتاب الآثار (۳) کتاب الرد علی سیر الاوزاعی غیر مطبوعہ کتابیں متعدد ہیں جیسے مبسوط امالی وغیرہ۔ امام ابو عبد الله محمد بن الحسن شیبانی رحمہ اللہ (واست؟ ۱۸۹ھ) امام اعظم کے خاص تلمیذ اور ان کے علوم کے جامع اور ناشر ہیں۔ امام اعظم کی وفات کے بعد امام ابو یوسف سے تعلیم مکمل کی آپ کی مطبوعہ کتابیں یہ ہیں (1) کتاب الاصل (مبسوط) (۲) جامع کبیر (۳) جامع صغیر (۴) زیادات (۵) زیادات الزيادات (۶) کتاب الآثار (۷) شرح السير الكبير للمرضى (اصل کتاب طبع نہیں ہوئی) (۸) کتاب الحجہ علی اہل المدینه (۹) موطا محمد (۱۰) کتاب الامالی۔ غیر مطبوعہ کتابیں بھی متعدد ہیں۔

امام ابو بکر خصاف (موچی؟) احمد بن عمر شیبانی رحمہ اللہ (متوفی ۲۶۱؟) جلیل القدر حنفی فقیہ ہیں۔ قاضی خان فرماتے ہیں والخصاف كان كبيراً في العلم، يجوز الاقتداء به (شامی ج ۲ ص ۲۹۵) آپ کی دو کتابیں مطبوعہ ہیں ایک احکام الاوقاف دوسری کتاب الحیل۔ اور ادب القاضی مخطوطہ ہے باقی کتابیں مفقود ہیں۔ امام ابو جعفر احمد بن محمد بن سلامه از دی طحاوی رحمہ اللہ (۲۳۹ ف ۳۲۱ھ) مشہور حنفی فقیہ اور بڑے محدث ہیں۔ مصر کے طحا مقام میں پیدا ہوئے۔ امام شافعی کے تلمیذ رشید امام مزنی رحمہ اللہ کے بھانجے تھے۔ آپ کی مطبوعہ کتابیں یہ ہیں (۱) شرح معانی الآثار (طحاوی شریف) (۲) بیان مشکل الآثار (اس کتاب کا چوتھائی حصہ پانچ جلدوں میں طبع ہوا) (۳) مختصر الطحاوی (فقہ حنفی کا متن ہے۔ بہت سے علماء نے اس کی شرحیں لکھی ہیں) اور غیر مطبوعہ کتابیں بہت ہیں۔

امام ابو الحسن کرخی عبید اللہ بن حسین رحمہ اللہ (و ۲۷۰ ف ۳۴۰؟) مشہور حنفی فقیہ ہیں۔ امام طحاوی اور امام خصاف کے معاصر ہیں۔ کرخ جائے ولادت ہے وفات بغداد میں ہوئی ہے۔ آپ کی مطبوعہ کتاب صرف اصول الکرخی ہے۔ اس میں وہ اصول بیان کیے گئے ہیں جن پر فقہ حنفی کی جزئیات کا مدار ہے۔ آپ نے جامع صغیر اور جامع کبیر کی شرحیں بھی لکھی ہیں۔

شمس الائمہ عبد العزیز بن احمد بخاری حلوانی رحمہ اللہ (متوفی ۲۳۸؟) پانچویں صدی کے مشہور حنفی فقیہ ہیں۔ حلوئی (مٹھائی) کی طرف نسبت ہے اس لیے حلوائی (نون کے بجائے ہمزہ) سے بھی بولا جاتا ہے۔ آپ شمس الائمہ مرضی رحمہ اللہ کے استاذ ہیں۔ آپ کی مطبوعہ کوئی کتاب نہیں۔ غیر مطبوعہ یہ ہیں (۱) مبسوط (۲) فتاویٰ (۳) امام ابو یوسف کی ادب القاضی کی شرح۔

ابو بکر شمس الائمہ محمد بن احمد سرخسی رحمہ اللہ (متوفی ۳۸۳ھ) پانچویں صدی کے مشہور حنفی فقیہ ہیں۔ حلوائی رحمہ اللہ (19) کے تلمیذ رشید ہیں۔ آپ کی مشہور کتاب مبسوط میں جلدوں میں مطبوعہ ہے۔ علاوہ ازیں سیر کبیر کی شرح چار جلدوں میں، اصول سرخسی اور نکت شرح زیادات الزیادات بھی مطبوعہ ہیں اور غیر مطبوعہ میں شرح جامع کبیر اور شرح مختصر الطحاوی ہیں۔ ابو العسر فخر الاسلام علی بن محمد بزدوی رحمہ اللہ (و ۲۰۰ ھ ف ۲۸۲ھ) پانچویں صدی کے مشہور اصولی اور فقیہ ہیں۔ بزدہ کی طرف (جو نسف کے قریب ایک قلعہ ہے) نسبت ہے۔ اصول فقہ میں آپ کی کتاب اصول بزدوی مطبوعہ ہے اس کا اصل نام کنز الوصول ہے۔ آپ نے ایک مبسوط بھی لکھی ہے جو ہنوز مخطوطہ ہے۔ نوٹ: آپ کے بڑے بھائی صدر الاسلام ابو الیسر محمد بن محمد بزدوی رحمہ اللہ (متوفی ۲؟) بھی بہت بڑے حنفی فقیہ ہیں اور بہت سی کتابوں کے مصنف ہیں۔ ان کے سوانح نگاروں نے لکھا ہے کان امام الائمة على الاطلاق ملابتصانيفه بطون الاوراق فوائد بہیہ ص ۷۷۔ مگر آپ کی کوئی کتاب مطبوعہ نہیں ہے۔ دونوں بھائیوں کا سبق دقت و
How do you give a fatwa? 145 Commentary on Rasm al-Mufti. (5) The marginalia of Hidayah, famously by Ibn Kamal and Ibn al-Kamal. The four Imams are: (1) Imam al-A'zam Abu Hanifa Nu'man ibn Thabit Kufi, may Allah have mercy on him, born 80 AH, died 150 AH. (2) Imam Malik ibn Anas Madani, born 93 AH, died 179 AH. (3) Imam Muhammad ibn Idris al-Shafi'i al-Hashimi, born 150 AH, died 204 AH. (4) Imam Ahmad ibn Muhammad ibn Hanbal Baghdadi, born 164 AH, died 241 AH.

Imam Abu Yusuf Ya'qub ibn Ibrahim al-Ansari, al-Kufi al-Baghdadi (died 182 AH) is the greatest disciple of Imam al-A'zam and the teacher of Imam Muhammad. He served as judge during the time of Abbasid caliphs al-Mahdi and Harun al-Rashid. He was the first to be given the title Qadi al-Qudat. His published books include: (1) Kitab al-Kharaj, (2) Kitab al-Athar, (3) Kitab al-Radd 'ala Siyar al-Awza'i. He has numerous unpublished works such as al-Mabsut and al-Amali. Imam Abu 'Abd Allah Muhammad ibn al-Hasan al-Shaybani (died 189 AH) is a special student of Imam al-A'zam and the compiler and publisher of his sciences. After Imam al-A'zam's death, he completed his education under Imam Abu Yusuf. His published books: (1) Kitab al-Asl (al-Mabsut), (2) al-Jami' al-Kabir, (3) al-Jami' al-Saghir, (4) al-Ziyadat, (5) Ziyadat al-Ziyadat, (6) Kitab al-Athar, (7) Sharh al-Siyar al-Kabir (original not printed), (8) Kitab al-Hujjah 'ala Ahl al-Madinah, (9) Muwatta' Muhammad, (10) Kitab al-Amali. He also has many unpublished books.

Imam Abu Bakr al-Khassaf (the felt seller?) Ahmad ibn 'Umar al-Shaybani (died 261 AH) is a great Hanafi jurist. Qadi Khan said: 'al-Khassaf was great in knowledge, it is permissible to follow him' (Shami vol.2 p.295). His two published books are: Ahkam al-Awqaf and Kitab al-Hiyal. Adab al-Qadi is in manuscript; his other books are lost. Imam Abu Ja'far Ahmad ibn Muhammad ibn Salamah al-Azdi al-Tahawi (239-321 AH) is a famous Hanafi jurist and great hadith scholar. He was born in Taha, Egypt. He was the nephew of Imam al-Muzani, the distinguished student of Imam al-Shafi'i. His published books: (1) Sharh Ma'ani al-Athar (Tahawi Sharif), (2) Bayan Mushkil al-Athar (one-fourth published in five volumes), (3) Mukhtasar al-Tahawi (a text of Hanafi fiqh; many scholars wrote commentaries on it). He has many unpublished works.

Imam Abu al-Hasan al-Karkhi 'Ubayd Allah ibn al-Husayn (died 270?/340?) is a well-known Hanafi jurist. He was a contemporary of Imam al-Tahawi and Imam al-Khassaf. His birthplace was Karkh; he died in Baghdad. His only published book is Usul al-Karkhi, which contains principles upon which the details of Hanafi fiqh are based. He also wrote commentaries on al-Jami' al-Saghir and al-Jami' al-Kabir.

Shams al-A'imma 'Abd al-'Aziz ibn Ahmad al-Bukhari al-Halwani (died 238?) is a famous Hanafi jurist of the fifth century. He is attributed to halwa (sweets), so also pronounced as Halwa'i (with hamza instead of nun). He was the teacher of Shams al-A'imma al-Marwazi. He has no published books; his unpublished works include: (1) al-Mabsut, (2) Fatawa, (3) Commentary on Imam Abu Yusuf's Adab al-Qadi.

Abu Bakr Shams al-A'imma Muhammad ibn Ahmad al-Sarakhsi (died 383 AH) is a famous Hanafi jurist of the fifth century. He is a distinguished student of al-Halwani. His famous book al-Mabsut is published in several volumes. Additionally, Sharh al-Siyar al-Kabir in four volumes, Usul al-Sarakhsi, and Nuqat Sharh Ziyadat al-Ziyadat are published. Unpublished works include Sharh al-Jami' al-Kabir and Sharh Mukhtasar al-Tahawi. Abu al-'Usr Fakhr al-Islam 'Ali ibn Muhammad al-Bazdawi (died 200?/282 AH) is a famous usuli and jurist of the fifth century. His nisbah is to Bazdah (a fortress near Nasaf). His book Usul al-Bazdawi is published; its original name is Kanz al-Wusul. He also wrote a Mabsut which remains in manuscript. Note: His elder brother Sadr al-Islam Abu al-Yusr Muhammad ibn Muhammad al-Bazdawi (died 2?) was also a great Hanafi jurist and author of many books. His biographers wrote: 'He was the imam of imams absolutely, his works fill the interiors of papers' (Fawa'id Bahiyyah p.77). However, none of his books are published. Source pages p. 146

Commentary
This passage is a biographical survey from Sharh Rasm al-Mufti, a work on the methodology of issuing fatwas in the Hanafi school. The author lists major Hanafi jurists chronologically, giving their names, dates, significance, and key works. This is essential for a mufti to understand the chain of transmission (sanad) of Hanafi fiqh and the authority of different scholars. The passage begins by naming the four founding imams of Sunni fiqh, then focuses on Hanafi luminaries: Imam Abu Yusuf, the first chief judge (Qadi al-Qudat) and author of foundational works; Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani, the compiler of the six core books (Zahir al-Riwayah); Imam al-Khassaf, an expert on awqaf and legal stratagems; Imam al-Tahawi, famous for his hadith-based fiqh works; Imam al-Karkhi, who wrote usul al-fiqh principles; Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani and his student al-Sarakhsi, whose al-Mabsut is a major reference; and finally al-Bazdawi, whose Usul al-Bazdawi is a key text in Hanafi usul al-fiqh. The inclusion of both published and unpublished works helps students gauge the accessibility and weight of each scholar's contributions. This knowledge is crucial for a mufti when citing authorities in fatwas.

Key Terms
امام (imam): A respected leader in Islamic jurisprudence, often used for the founders of madhhabs or major scholars.
فقیہ (faqih): A jurist specialized in deriving legal rulings from the sources.
اصول فقہ (usul al-fiqh): The principles and methodology of deriving Islamic law, as developed by scholars like al-Karkhi and al-Bazdawi.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) Imam al-Tahawi

Key Takeaway
Knowing the biographical chain of Hanafi jurists and their key works is essential for a mufti to correctly navigate the school's authoritative sources.

Foundational Hanafi Scholars and Their Printed Works
Listing major Hanafi scholars and their key works

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify seven major Hanafi scholars and list their key printed works used in fatwa issuance.

Core Idea
Knowing which scholar wrote which printed text is essential for fatwa reference and reliability.

This biographical passage introduces seven Hanafi scholars, ranging from the 3rd to 6th centuries AH, highlighting their celebrated printed works. As a mufti, understanding who authored the texts you consult helps you assess authority and transmission strength. The passage also distinguishes printed books from manuscripts, a crucial factor in determining textual availability.

Guided Path
1
Identify the seven scholars
Locate the seven numbered entries (18–24). Write each scholar's full name and death date (if given).
Numbers are approximate in the original due to OCR; focus on names and works.
2
List their printed works
For each scholar, pick out the works explicitly listed as 'matbu'ah' (printed). Note the title and any special significance (e.g., 'Usul al-Karkhi' is the foundation of Hanafi fiqh).
Printed works are more readily available and often form the core curriculum.
3
Understand the role of al-Karkhi's Usul
The passage states that Usul al-Karkhi contains the principles (usul) upon which the details (juz'iyyat) of Hanafi fiqh rest (مدار). Commit this to memory as it explains the work's centrality.
This is a key chain between usul and furu'.

How do you give a fatwa? 146 Commentary on Rasm al-Mufti is (3) Mukhtasar al-Tahawi (it is a text of Hanafi fiqh. Many scholars have written commentaries on it) and unprinted books are many. -IA Imam Abu al-Hasan al-Karkhi 'Ubayd Allah ibn Husayn, may Allah have mercy on him (d. 270? d. 340?) is a famous Hanafi jurist. He is a contemporary of Imam al-Tahawi and Imam al-Khassaf. Karkh is his birthplace, he died in Baghdad. His only printed book is Usul al-Karkhi. In it are stated those principles on which the details of Hanafi fiqh are based. He also wrote commentaries on Jami' al-Saghir and Jami' al-Kabir. -19 Shams al-A'imma 'Abd al-'Aziz ibn Ahmad Bukhari Halwani, may Allah have mercy on him (d. 238?) is a famous Hanafi jurist of the fifth century. He is attributed to halwa (sweets), so it is also pronounced Halwa'i (with hamza instead of nun). He is the teacher of Shams al-A'imma al-Marzi, may Allah have mercy on him. He has no printed book. His unprinted works are: (1) al-Mabsut (2) Fatawa (3) Commentary on Adab al-Qadi of Imam Abu Yusuf. -20 Abu Bakr Shams al-A'imma Muhammad ibn Ahmad al-Sarakhsi, may Allah have mercy on him (d. 383 AH) is a famous Hanafi jurist of the fifth century. He is the distinguished student of Halwani (19). His famous book al-Mabsut is printed in [many] volumes. In addition, the commentary on al-Siyar al-Kabir in four volumes, Usul al-Sarakhsi, and Nuqt Sharh Ziyadat al-Ziyadat are also printed, and among the unprinted are Sharh Jami' al-Kabir and Sharh Mukhtasar al-Tahawi. Abu al-'Usr Fakhr al-Islam 'Ali ibn Muhammad al-Bazdawi, may Allah have mercy on him (d. 200? or 282 AH?) is a famous usuli and jurist of the fifth century. He is attributed to Bazda (which is a fortress near Nasaf). His book Usul al-Bazdawi in usul al-fiqh is printed; its original name is Kanz al-Wusul. He also wrote a Mabsut which is still in manuscript. Note: His elder brother Sadr al-Islam Abu al-Yusr Muhammad ibn Muhammad al-Bazdawi, may Allah have mercy on him (d. 2?) is also a very great Hanafi jurist and author of many books. His biographers wrote: 'He was the imam of imams absolutely; the folds of papers were filled with his books' (Fawa'id Bahiyya p. 77), but none of his books are printed. The teaching of the two brothers was completely different in profundity and ease. The elder brother's style of expression was smooth, lucid, and clear, so he was called Abu al-Yusr, and the younger brother's was precise, so the students called him Abu al-'Usr. 22 - 'Allama Fakhr al-Din Qadi Hasan ibn Mansur Uzjandi, Farghani, may Allah have mercy on him (d. 596 AH) is a famous Hanafi jurist of the sixth century. His Fatawa Qadi Khan, which is also called al-Khaniyya, is printed on the margin of Fatawa 'Alamgiri, and his unprinted books are: (1) Amali (2) Sharh Ziyadat (3) Sharh Jami' al-Saghir (4) Commentary on Adab al-Qadi of al-Khassaf. Uzjand is a place near Farghana. 23- Imam Abu Bakr al-Jassas Ahmad ibn 'Ali al-Razi, may Allah have mercy on him (b. 305 AH, d. 537 AH) is a famous Hanafi jurist, exegete, and usuli scholar. His famous book Ahkam al-Qur'an is printed in five volumes. He also has a significant work in usul al-fiqh, which is still in manuscript. 24- Imam al-Quduri Abu al-Husayn Ahmad ibn Muhammad, may Allah have mercy on him (b. 364? d. 328? AH) is a famous Hanafi jurist of the fourth century. His blessed and famous book Mukhtasar al-Quduri is a printed textbook. In polemics (khilafiyat), he also has a book al-Tajrid, which is in manuscript.
Source pages p. 147

Commentary
This passage is a biographical section listing Hanafi scholars and their works. It begins with a reference to Mukhtasar al-Tahawi as a core text, then proceeds to introduce seven scholars (numbered 18-24 in the original list). Each entry provides the scholar's full name, dates (often approximate), notable teachers/students, and a list of their printed and unprinted works. The focus is on identifying authoritative sources in the Hanafi school, especially those that are foundational for fatwa issuance. The entries highlight the scholarly chain, such as al-Halwani being the teacher of al-Sarakhsi, and the Bazdawi brothers' differing styles. This serves as a reference for students of ifta to know the key figures and their contributions.

Key Terms
مطبوعہ (matbu'ah): Printed/published books as opposed to manuscripts.
غیر مطبوعہ (ghayr matbu'ah): Unprinted books, existing only in manuscript form.
مدار (madar): The basis or foundation upon which the details (juz'iyyat) of Hanafi fiqh rest.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Knowing the printed works of early Hanafi scholars like al-Sarakhsi, al-Karkhi, and al-Quduri is essential for building a reliable fatwa reference library.

The Hanafi Scholarly Network: Teachers, Students, and Transmission
Listing major Hanafi scholars and their key works

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to trace the teacher-student relationships among the listed Hanafi scholars and explain the difference in the Bazdawi brothers' teaching styles.

Core Idea
The Hanafi school's strength lies in its documented chains of transmission from teacher to student.

Beyond listing works, this passage reveals the scholarly connections that preserved and transmitted Hanafi fiqh. Noting who taught whom — such as al-Halwani teaching al-Sarakhsi — helps us understand how ideas and texts evolved. The Bazdawi brothers' contrasting styles show how personal methodology shaped reception.

Guided Path
1
Map teacher-student pairs
From the passage, identify at least two clear teacher-student relationships: al-Halwani → al-Sarakhsi, and note that al-Halwani was also the teacher of al-Marzi. Also, note that al-Karkhi was a contemporary of al-Tahawi and al-Khassaf.
Not all entries explicitly mention teachers; focus on what is given.
2
Analyze the Bazdawi brothers contrast
Read the note about the two brothers: Sadr al-Islam (Abu al-Yusr) and Fakhr al-Islam (Abu al-'Usr). Understand why students called them 'Abu al-Yusr' (father of ease) and 'Abu al-'Usr' (father of difficulty).
This contrast illustrates that personal teaching style affects how knowledge is transmitted.
3
Assess the role of unprinted works in the chain
Notice that several scholars have unprinted works. For example, al-Halwani's works are only in manuscript, yet he was a key teacher. Reflect on how unprinted works still influence the school through their students' writings.
Unprinted does not mean uninfluential.

How do you give a fatwa? 146 Commentary on Rasm al-Mufti is (3) Mukhtasar al-Tahawi (it is a text of Hanafi fiqh. Many scholars have written commentaries on it) and unprinted books are many. -IA Imam Abu al-Hasan al-Karkhi 'Ubayd Allah ibn Husayn, may Allah have mercy on him (d. 270? d. 340?) is a famous Hanafi jurist. He is a contemporary of Imam al-Tahawi and Imam al-Khassaf. Karkh is his birthplace, he died in Baghdad. His only printed book is Usul al-Karkhi. In it are stated those principles on which the details of Hanafi fiqh are based. He also wrote commentaries on Jami' al-Saghir and Jami' al-Kabir. -19 Shams al-A'imma 'Abd al-'Aziz ibn Ahmad Bukhari Halwani, may Allah have mercy on him (d. 238?) is a famous Hanafi jurist of the fifth century. He is attributed to halwa (sweets), so it is also pronounced Halwa'i (with hamza instead of nun). He is the teacher of Shams al-A'imma al-Marzi, may Allah have mercy on him. He has no printed book. His unprinted works are: (1) al-Mabsut (2) Fatawa (3) Commentary on Adab al-Qadi of Imam Abu Yusuf. -20 Abu Bakr Shams al-A'imma Muhammad ibn Ahmad al-Sarakhsi, may Allah have mercy on him (d. 383 AH) is a famous Hanafi jurist of the fifth century. He is the distinguished student of Halwani (19). His famous book al-Mabsut is printed in [many] volumes. In addition, the commentary on al-Siyar al-Kabir in four volumes, Usul al-Sarakhsi, and Nuqt Sharh Ziyadat al-Ziyadat are also printed, and among the unprinted are Sharh Jami' al-Kabir and Sharh Mukhtasar al-Tahawi. Abu al-'Usr Fakhr al-Islam 'Ali ibn Muhammad al-Bazdawi, may Allah have mercy on him (d. 200? or 282 AH?) is a famous usuli and jurist of the fifth century. He is attributed to Bazda (which is a fortress near Nasaf). His book Usul al-Bazdawi in usul al-fiqh is printed; its original name is Kanz al-Wusul. He also wrote a Mabsut which is still in manuscript. Note: His elder brother Sadr al-Islam Abu al-Yusr Muhammad ibn Muhammad al-Bazdawi, may Allah have mercy on him (d. 2?) is also a very great Hanafi jurist and author of many books. His biographers wrote: 'He was the imam of imams absolutely; the folds of papers were filled with his books' (Fawa'id Bahiyya p. 77), but none of his books are printed. The teaching of the two brothers was completely different in profundity and ease. The elder brother's style of expression was smooth, lucid, and clear, so he was called Abu al-Yusr, and the younger brother's was precise, so the students called him Abu al-'Usr. 22 - 'Allama Fakhr al-Din Qadi Hasan ibn Mansur Uzjandi, Farghani, may Allah have mercy on him (d. 596 AH) is a famous Hanafi jurist of the sixth century. His Fatawa Qadi Khan, which is also called al-Khaniyya, is printed on the margin of Fatawa 'Alamgiri, and his unprinted books are: (1) Amali (2) Sharh Ziyadat (3) Sharh Jami' al-Saghir (4) Commentary on Adab al-Qadi of al-Khassaf. Uzjand is a place near Farghana. 23- Imam Abu Bakr al-Jassas Ahmad ibn 'Ali al-Razi, may Allah have mercy on him (b. 305 AH, d. 537 AH) is a famous Hanafi jurist, exegete, and usuli scholar. His famous book Ahkam al-Qur'an is printed in five volumes. He also has a significant work in usul al-fiqh, which is still in manuscript. 24- Imam al-Quduri Abu al-Husayn Ahmad ibn Muhammad, may Allah have mercy on him (b. 364? d. 328? AH) is a famous Hanafi jurist of the fourth century. His blessed and famous book Mukhtasar al-Quduri is a printed textbook. In polemics (khilafiyat), he also has a book al-Tajrid, which is in manuscript.
Source pages p. 147

Commentary
This passage is a biographical section listing Hanafi scholars and their works. It begins with a reference to Mukhtasar al-Tahawi as a core text, then proceeds to introduce seven scholars (numbered 18-24 in the original list). Each entry provides the scholar's full name, dates (often approximate), notable teachers/students, and a list of their printed and unprinted works. The focus is on identifying authoritative sources in the Hanafi school, especially those that are foundational for fatwa issuance. The entries highlight the scholarly chain, such as al-Halwani being the teacher of al-Sarakhsi, and the Bazdawi brothers' differing styles. This serves as a reference for students of ifta to know the key figures and their contributions.

Key Terms
مطبوعہ (matbu'ah): Printed/published books as opposed to manuscripts.
غیر مطبوعہ (ghayr matbu'ah): Unprinted books, existing only in manuscript form.
مدار (madar): The basis or foundation upon which the details (juz'iyyat) of Hanafi fiqh rest.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Tracing teacher-student chains in Hanafi biographical works is essential for understanding the transmission and authority of legal rulings.

Foundational Hanafi Jurists for Fatwa Methodology
Biographical introduction to foundational Hanafi jurists and their key texts.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the major Hanafi jurists introduced in this passage and state the significance of their works for fatwa practice.

Core Idea
Knowing key Hanafi scholars and their works is essential for assessing fatwa authority.

The Hanafi school possesses a rich legacy of scholars whose works form the bedrock of fatwa issuance. This lesson introduces several luminaries—ranging from jurists to usuli experts—whose contributions are frequently cited in fatwa manuals. Understanding their roles helps a mufti navigate the hierarchy of sources and apply the correct rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scholars
Read the passage and list the four distinct scholars mentioned: the two brothers (Abu Aysar and Abu al-Usr), Fakhr al-Din Qadi Khan, Abu Bakr al-Jassas, and Imam al-Quduri.
The brothers are mentioned as a pair, but each had a distinct style.
2
Note their key works
For each scholar, identify the work(s) attributed to them. For example, Fatawa Qadi Khan for Qadi Khan, Ahkam al-Qur'an for al-Jassas, Mukhtasar al-Quduri for al-Quduri.
Pay attention to which works are published and which remain in manuscript.
3
Understand the relevance to fatwa
Reflect on how each work contributes to fatwa methodology: al-Quduri's Mukhtasar is a concise fiqh matn, al-Jassas's Ahkam al-Qur'an is a tafsir ahkam used for deriving rules, Qadi Khan's Fatawa is a collection of legal opinions, and the brothers' styles illustrate different approaches to fatwa writing.
This diversity shows the range of sources a mufti must master.
4
Recognize the hierarchy of authority
Understand that later Hanafi fatwa literature often relies on specific scholars like Qadi Khan and al-Quduri as primary references, while usuli works like those of al-Jassas support the methodology.
This hierarchy is part of Rasm al-Mufti—knowing whom to cite.
